The Gemera is a mid-engine two-seater car that can fit four full grown-ups without compromising the experience. It took years to figure out how to make this possible, and the production version was presented in 2020. To make it work, the team had to innovate new types of drivetrain, technologies, and design. The car is capable of running in E motor mode on all four wheels simultaneously or on the front or rear axle with full torque vectoring. Additionally, the team created a three cylinder TFG version with 1,400 horsepower and a YESCO V8 engine with 2,300 horsepower and 2,850 Newton meters of torque. The car also has creature comforts and function systems, infotainment systems, and hot and cold cup holders.  Key themes: 1. Innovative drivetrain, technologies, and design 2. High performance engine options 3. Creature comforts and function systems

What I really appreciate about Koenigsegg is how transparent they are with their innovations. I have been following the Gemera since launch and had been following Koenigsegg's evolution closely since the CCX days, so I was familiar with the acting principles of the Regera derived torque converter present in the early Gemera. When Christian opened with how the team had worked on integrating the "LST" into the car but ran into packaging issues, In that moment I was thinking about how one would tackle this problem. My first thought was exploiting the operating mechanism of the LST,(the many clutch system allows for unique packaging as no longer need all gears on one shaft) so when Christian said that they resolved this through this "Turbulone system" I had a wonderful "AHA!" moment where I understood what they did, something which could never have happened if Koenigsegg hadn't explained how the LST works in great detail with the release of the Jesko. I truly felt like I was being brought along the path of innovation with Koenigsegg and sharing their triumphs with them, like how one might feel when your football team won the championship; they were sharing the victory with us by allowing us to understand why each innovation was possible. It's for this reason that I can't bring myself to feel anything but fondness for them, because I'm so smitten for this collective of mad scientists I'm not even mad that I could never realistically own one. (Not that I won't be trying)

Originally it was a big electric motor RWD, petrol engine FWD car, which on paper sounded impressive, 1700hp AWD, but the problem is that if the batteries run out of power while you were driving it on track, then the car became a 600hp FWD car, which would handle horribly.
